  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_10000d01-61fd-4456-a0eb-250bc7146fb3'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18320504629074949147">Eight centuries ago the first Knight of the Word was commissioned to combat the demonic evil of the Void. Now that daunting legacy has passed to John Ross - along with powerful magic and the knowledge that his actions are all that stand between a living hell and humanity's future.<br/>Then, after decades of service to the Word, an unspeakable act of violence shatters John Ross'</span>
  <span id="freeText18320504629074949147" style="display:none">Eight centuries ago the first Knight of the Word was commissioned to combat the demonic evil of the Void. Now that daunting legacy has passed to John Ross - along with powerful magic and the knowledge that his actions are all that stand between a living hell and humanity's future.<br />Then, after decades of service to the Word, an unspeakable act of violence shatters John Ross's weary faith. Haunted by guilt, he turns his back on his dread gift, settling down to build a normal life, untroubled by demons and nightmares.<br />But a fallen Knight makes a tempting prize for the Void, which could bend the Knight's magic to its own evil ends. And once the demons on Ross's trail track him to Seattle, neither he nor anyone close to him will be safe. His only hope is Nest Freemark, a college student who wields an extraordinary magic all her own. Five years earlier, Ross had aided Nest when the future of humanity rested upon her choice between Word and Void. Now Nest must return the favor. She must restore Ross's faith, or his life - and hers - will be forfeit...</span>
  <a data-text-id="18320504629074949147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124090868" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2763719-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564310959p2/2763719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124090868?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/2763719-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124090868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16197525057251347043">Brooks' uninspired and often tedious novel Running With The Demon gets a follow-up novel that continues to try readers' patience without actually being bad enough to make them give up on it entirely. In Knight of the Word, the novel's main character must undergo the kind of crisis of faith that we've seen before in countless books and films of every genre. Namely, the hero's special powers prove unable to save absolutely everybody who comes within harm's way, burdening the hero with an abundance</span>
  <span id="freeText16197525057251347043" style="display:none">Brooks' uninspired and often tedious novel Running With The Demon gets a follow-up novel that continues to try readers' patience without actually being bad enough to make them give up on it entirely. In Knight of the Word, the novel's main character must undergo the kind of crisis of faith that we've seen before in countless books and films of every genre. Namely, the hero's special powers prove unable to save absolutely everybody who comes within harm's way, burdening the hero with an abundance of unwarranted guilt and causing him to attempt to shrug off the mantle of being a hero in exchange for a normal life. Predictability ensues. Unfortunately, Brooks makes his hero so wrought with indisiciveness that he loses his "cool" cred and ultimately becomes rather annoying and unlikable. The mystery aspect of the story isn't really much of a mystery, and the fantasy elements aren't brought into play as often or explored with as much depth as I would have liked. One of Brook's weakest novels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16197525057251347043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108940322" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8923240079667362388">Number two in the Terry Brooks urban fantasy series doesn't disappoint. I didn't like it quite as much as the first, but it was pretty close. <br/><br/>This has more "urban" as it goes from small town Illinois in the fist book to Seattle in this one. And once there, one must wonder just how many times the characters will stop for Starbucks. Nobody listened to Nirvana in this though (that happened in the first book), so it wasn't too bad for Seattle stereotypes. It did mention the Kingdome a couple of time</span>
  <span id="freeText8923240079667362388" style="display:none">Number two in the Terry Brooks urban fantasy series doesn't disappoint. I didn't like it quite as much as the first, but it was pretty close. <br /><br />This has more "urban" as it goes from small town Illinois in the fist book to Seattle in this one. And once there, one must wonder just how many times the characters will stop for Starbucks. Nobody listened to Nirvana in this though (that happened in the first book), so it wasn't too bad for Seattle stereotypes. It did mention the Kingdome a couple of times. That's a bit dated, but as a longtime Broncos fan, I remember that as a scary place.<br /><br />But back to the story. This happens 5 years after the first book, and we have an all grown up Nest Freemark going to Seattle to knock some sense into John Ross, the Knight of the Word who has lost his way. <br /><br />And where do we go from here, but to <i>Angel Fire East</i>. Looking forward to that.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15504613911701071007"> #2/29 in my Epic Shannara Quest.<br/><br/>This sequel to <i>Running with the Demon</i> doesn't disappoint. It's full of intense, sometimes scary scenes, plenty of exciting action and mystery. If it seems uninspired compared to it's predecessor, <i>A Knight of the Word</i>, this book makes up for it by moving the setting from small-town Illinois to urban Seattle (which Brooks paints in vivid and loving detail) and giving this series social conscience.<br/><br/>The mythos behind the world that ultimately becomes Shannara is becom</span>
  <span id="freeText15504613911701071007" style="display:none"> #2/29 in my Epic Shannara Quest.<br /><br />This sequel to <i>Running with the Demon</i> doesn't disappoint. It's full of intense, sometimes scary scenes, plenty of exciting action and mystery. If it seems uninspired compared to it's predecessor, <i>A Knight of the Word</i>, this book makes up for it by moving the setting from small-town Illinois to urban Seattle (which Brooks paints in vivid and loving detail) and giving this series social conscience.<br /><br />The mythos behind the world that ultimately becomes Shannara is becoming fascinatingly complex as Brooks moves his saga briskly along. I'm looking forward to the final book of <i>The Word and the Void</i> trilogy as well as the next chapter in the Shannara epic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15504613911701071007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText6886017200583491147" style="display:none">The middle book in the trilogy of when Shannara was still our earth. The events are leading up to apocalypse, can the Knight of the Word stop it? Not when he has denied his calling and the void is starting to win. Luckily he has an old friend watching his back.<br /><br />I didn't like this quite as much as the first novel, I figured out the bad guy from literally the first appearance, and there was a lot of the feeling of an extended chase scene about the whole thing. Still, worth a read though, if you are interested in how we became Shannara. And this one takes place full on in downtown Seattle, so bonus points there.</span>

<div id="review_838025668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838025668" />
    <a title="MC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28164369-mc"><img alt="MC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483779945p2/28164369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838025668?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MC" href="/user/show/28164369-mc">MC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5461956-a-knight-of-the-word">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838025668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3487715313947472157"><i>A Knight of the Word</i>, the second book in Terry Brooks' <i>The Word and the Void</i> trilogy changes around some of the actors. We still have Nest, John Ross and O'olish Amaneh, but in this situation John Ross is the one in danger of falling to the Void, Nest must convince him to turn back to the Word and Two Bears (Amaneh) is ready to kill him if he might fall.<br/><br/>The action begins five years after the first book, <i>Running with the Demon</i>, with Nest mourning the death of her grandfather, Bob Freemark. She ha</span>
  <span id="freeText3487715313947472157" style="display:none"><i>A Knight of the Word</i>, the second book in Terry Brooks' <i>The Word and the Void</i> trilogy changes around some of the actors. We still have Nest, John Ross and O'olish Amaneh, but in this situation John Ross is the one in danger of falling to the Void, Nest must convince him to turn back to the Word and Two Bears (Amaneh) is ready to kill him if he might fall.<br /><br />The action begins five years after the first book, <i>Running with the Demon</i>, with Nest mourning the death of her grandfather, Bob Freemark. She has choices to make about whether to sell her house, and is struggling with balancing her dreams and her duties to serve the Word, when she recieves news about Ross.<br /><br />You see, after a horrific failure for which Ross blames himself, he has decided to stop being a Knight of the Word, and is trying to ignore that previous life. But the cosmology of the series is clear that he can not just give up the magic or calling, only the Word can release him. Therefore, he is traveling around, trying to live his attempt at a "normal life" with the magic still at his disposal, though hidden away and sleeping, as it were. He is ripe for being turned to the service of the Void.<br /><br />Nest is told all of this and warned he will be killed to prevent his fall from grace, if it is necessary. To head this off, she agrees to travel to Seattle, Washington, where Ross now lives and works at a nationally-recognized charity, and convince him of the danger posed to him.<br /><br />And once there, she finds Ross embroiled in a complicated series of clever manipulations designed to subvert him and turn to the service of evil.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this story. It didn't have the same feel of epicness as the first <i>Running</i> did, but it did have a sense of a mystery. In fact, that is how I'll describe them both. Whereas <i>Running</i> was an epic fantasy in an urban fantasy format, <i>Knight</i> seemed to be more of a standard mystery-oriented urban fantasy. <br /><br />Of course, in a way this was inevitable, given the plot of subverting John Ross and taking place in one of the major US cities versus a family saga in a small town surrounded by lush landscapes. It was no less enjoyable.<br /><br />One of the parts that struck me was how Brooks brings up issues that we don't think about to feed into the notions of the never ending battle of the Word and the Void, creation and entropy, that are standard to his trilogy. He also had me at least a little empathizing with John choosing the wrong choice, because it's hard not to like John, to feel sad for him and understand that he wants some happiness.<br /><br />Nest, for her part, is in a part of her life where she is trying to decide between past and future, what to give up or not give up of her life so far. Sorrows, fears, so forth, are her companions. But hope is too. Watching her struggle with her emotions and choose what to do, how to find meaning in life, was poignant and just as important and impactful as observing John Ross' struggle.<br /><br />Sure, Brooks can navel-gaze somewhat, but in general, he does do a good job on characterization and of helping the readers understand his characters' thoughts, motives, fears, so forth.<br /><br />A great book that has me looking forward to the final book soon.<br /><br />Highly Recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3487715313947472157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1944320630424645303">In way I like this better then the first book in the series because now I was more familiar with the authors world and Nest is more grown, however, at time this was little predicable. <br/><br/>My main issue and I could be wrong here is that Nest figures out who the daemon is by how the daemon acted around Ross and that it was similar to how the other daemon acted around Gran. However Nest, Ross, and the daemon were never in the same place. The first time Nest and Ross meet she is outside when he comes up</span>
  <span id="freeText1944320630424645303" style="display:none">In way I like this better then the first book in the series because now I was more familiar with the authors world and Nest is more grown, however, at time this was little predicable. <br /><br />My main issue and I could be wrong here is that Nest figures out who the daemon is by how the daemon acted around Ross and that it was similar to how the other daemon acted around Gran. However Nest, Ross, and the daemon were never in the same place. The first time Nest and Ross meet she is outside when he comes up in a Taxi and the second he meets her in her hotel lobby. And both time they depart from each abruptly and no one else is with them. Also I don't recall Gran, other daemon and Nest hanging out. Ok as the reader, the Daemon's ID is little predicable and you don't need Nest's thinking about Gran to figure it out. <br /><br />Also this book could have more meat. I'd like to see Two Bears kick some ass. I think Nest could have another episode where she demonstrated a more mature use of magic. Also this daemon wasn't as calculating as the first. There should have been some more misdirection and manipulation.<br /><br />Anyway this book was good enough that I stayed up rather late finish it. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1596500663" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13477515-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349717088p2/13477515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1596500663?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/13477515-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1596500663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10577983375327469397">I avoided the Shannarra series for years in deference to Tolkien, but finally picked up Running with the Demon since Terry Brooks is from my home town and based the story there. That book was a bit of a slog but showed enough that i decided to continue the series. A Knight of the Word is a writing of the highest level. Fast paced, intricate, fluid. The foreshadowing led me to conclusions early that proved true but did not take away from the story as it played out. <br/><br/>I am now a Terry Brooks convert</span>
  <span id="freeText10577983375327469397" style="display:none">I avoided the Shannarra series for years in deference to Tolkien, but finally picked up Running with the Demon since Terry Brooks is from my home town and based the story there. That book was a bit of a slog but showed enough that i decided to continue the series. A Knight of the Word is a writing of the highest level. Fast paced, intricate, fluid. The foreshadowing led me to conclusions early that proved true but did not take away from the story as it played out. <br /><br />I am now a Terry Brooks convert. If you ever read anything of his, read chapter 13 of this book. He wrote it in 1998; I thought he was writing about current world situations as I read it. It's timeless. </span>

<div id="review_3448313822" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3448313822" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1777325-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413646019p2/1777325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3448313822?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/1777325-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1777325-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3448313822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer117515439567326864"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420496.A_Knight_of_the_Word__Word___Void___2_' title='A Knight of the Word (Word & Void, #2) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Knight of the Word</a> follows Brooks' <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_' title='Running with the Demon (Word & Void, #1) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Running with the Demon</a>, moving the focus to John Ross. I tend to agree with Rebecca Fisher, from the FANTASY LITERATURE website, who offers her insights below. (Fisher earned a Masters degree in literature at the University of Canterbury in New Zealand. )<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/a-knight-of-the-word/'>http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a><br/><br/>"The basic premise is a good against evil plot, embodied in the forces known as the Word and the Void. Both sides have creatures loyal to them, namely demons on behalf </span>
  <span id="freeText117515439567326864" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420496.A_Knight_of_the_Word__Word___Void___2_" title="A Knight of the Word (Word &amp; Void, #2) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">A Knight of the Word</a> follows Brooks' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_" title="Running with the Demon (Word &amp; Void, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Running with the Demon</a>, moving the focus to John Ross. I tend to agree with Rebecca Fisher, from the FANTASY LITERATURE website, who offers her insights below. (Fisher earned a Masters degree in literature at the University of Canterbury in New Zealand. )<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/a-knight-of-the-word/">http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a><br /><br />"The basic premise is a good against evil plot, embodied in the forces known as the Word and the Void. Both sides have creatures loyal to them, namely demons on behalf of the Void, and Knights for the Word. The present Knight of the Word is a man named John Ross, who lives a lonely existence; wandering an post-apocalyptic future in his dreams in order to find clues and answers to what transpired to prevent it from happening in the present.<br /><br />Anyway, after a botched rescue mission that results in the deaths of several children, Ross gives up his calling and settles down to a new life. He has a girlfriend, Stefanie Winslow, and they both work for “the Wizard of Oz”, the nickname given to Simon Lawrence, a charity worker for homeless people. Meanwhile, the magically inclined Nest Freemark (the young girl that Ross saved in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_" title="Running with the Demon (Word &amp; Void, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Running with the Demon</a>) is now nineteen years old and in a rut in her life.<br /><br />All seems reasonably well, but the Word’s messenger, a tatterdemalion named Arial, assures Nest that Ross has made himself vulnerable to the Void by ignoring his calling, and only Nest can make him aware of a demon in his presence attempting to corrupt him. Meanwhile, back in Seattle, an investigative reporter named Andrew Wren is uncovering suspicious facts that may prove the downfall of Lawrence’s foundation and Ross’s work.<br /><br />It is a solid enough sequel, but not up to par with its predecessor. I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_" title="Running with the Demon (Word &amp; Void, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Running with the Demon</a> immensely due to its environment (the far-reaching parklands) and the supporting cast. Here, however, most of the old cast has died or moved on: Cass Minter and Old Bob have died, Brianna and Jared have moved away, and even the cats are gone. Brooks may be attempting to make the situation true to life, but it comes across as rather depressing. Despite the presence of Robert, Nest feels very much alone in this book, with none of the hope and promise that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_" title="Running with the Demon (Word &amp; Void, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Running with the Demon</a> concluded with....<br /><br />I found that Nest was the more interesting character out of the two protagonists, though I can’t exactly pinpoint why, and I liked the way the roles had been reversed from the previous book — now Nest is the rescuer. Likewise, Arial was an interesting idea (a spirit made up of lost children’s memories) and it was fun to see another sylvan — Boot. But I have to admit that unlike other reviewers, the secret identity of the demon did catch me off guard."<br /><br />This book is more somber than the first in the series, since it's set in the world of Seattle's homeless population. I respect Brooks' efforts to raise awareness of the plight of the homeless, especially since the demons are hunting them down. But the bond between Ross and Nest isn't as clear as it was in Hopewell--and they go their separate ways at the end. <br /><br />I know there is a third book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15558.Angel_Fire_East__Word___Void___3_" title="Angel Fire East (Word &amp; Void, #3) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Fire East</a>, but I'm not going to re-read it now. So many books, so little time--especially when I'm nearing 80!</span>
  <a data-text-id="117515439567326864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeremy Michael Gallen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeremy Michael Gallen" href="/user/show/35009294-jeremy-michael-gallen">Jeremy Michael Gallen</a>

        rated it

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174076763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5717902032528804587">In the first sequel to Running with the Demon and second installment of author Terry Brooks’ Word and Void trilogy, distant prequels to his main Shannara pantheon, the titular Knight of the Word, John Ross, has a post-doomsday vision of the future in Seattle, with an accusatory old man, Ross now leaving behind his duty to the Word to work in the Washington city for a homeless shelter known as Fresh Start, being speechwriter to Simon Lawrence, who bears the nickname The Wizard of Oz for his help </span>
  <span id="freeText5717902032528804587" style="display:none">In the first sequel to Running with the Demon and second installment of author Terry Brooks’ Word and Void trilogy, distant prequels to his main Shannara pantheon, the titular Knight of the Word, John Ross, has a post-doomsday vision of the future in Seattle, with an accusatory old man, Ross now leaving behind his duty to the Word to work in the Washington city for a homeless shelter known as Fresh Start, being speechwriter to Simon Lawrence, who bears the nickname The Wizard of Oz for his help of the community’s disadvantaged.<br /><br />In Hopewell, Illinois, hometown of protagonist Nest Freemark, both her grandparents are now deceased, Gran for five years and Old Bob a few months before. She is nineteen and in college, receiving offers for her grandparents’ abode, confiding in her sylvan friend Pick, and attracting affection from her friend Robert Keppler, who visits all the way from California. Pick indicates that someone is in Sinnissippi park to talk with her, turning out to be a tatterdemalion named Ariel who indicates that John Ross has fallen from grace, abandoning his duties as a Knight of a Word due to his failure to prevent a tragedy in San Sobel, near San Francisco.<br /><br />On Monday, October 29, John Ross prepares a speech for his superior Simon Lawrence, whom he is allegedly supposed to kill in two days in accordance with his visions. A new character is a journalist from The New York Times named Andrew Wren, who is skeptical of the so-called Wizard of Oz, finding improprieties in his programs for the impoverished, confronting Lawrence and receiving some influence from an unidentified demon. Ross, content in his new position, travels to Wales to renounce himself as a Knight of the Word, although he fails to find the Fairy Glen where it was supposed to be. He is also in a relationship with fellow employee Stefanie Winslow.<br /><br />On Tuesday, October 30, Nest arrives in Seattle in hopes of convincing Ross not to renounce his position, although she fails, soon after which he meets her old Native American friend Two Bears, who assures Nest that it is her destiny to convince Ross to remain a Knight of the Word, and disappears with little to no trace. Ariel, who has grater magic capacity as a tatterdemalion than sylvans such as Pick, manages to show up in Seattle, with some new friends including the sylvan Boot and his owl and primary mode of transportation Audrey. The demon, shortly afterward, strikes, with Nest ultimately returning to her hotel and pondering her next course of action.<br /><br />On Wednesday, October 31, further tragedy strikes the Fresh Start homeless shelter in the form of a fire, with the mentioned demon the possible arsonist, and the mystery of its true identity providing a decent drive to follow the book through to the end. The identity of the demon does indeed come to light, and Ross’s decision of whether to remain a Knight of the Word is pondered. Overall, this is an enjoyable sequel that hits most of the right notes, although there is occasional similarity to Star Wars, with the Void tempting Ross away from his service to the Word, but even so, those that enjoyed the first entry will most likely enjoy the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5717902032528804587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2337814043" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2337814043" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13681753-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474085415p2/13681753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2337814043?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/13681753-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13681753-christine?shelf=real-world-fantasy">real-world-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337814043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8125403743820812196">This is the second installment in The Word and Void series, and that defines it a little. It is like the third act of any story and gets correspondingly dark. You know, like The Empire Strikes Back. <br/><br/>However, I can't decide whether I find John Ross's crisis believable or not. Part of me says that it is over-dramatic and unrealistic for the character that we are introduced to in Running with the Demon to become so self-deceived and self-indulgent and just so plain stupid and pig-headed as John is </span>
  <span id="freeText8125403743820812196" style="display:none">This is the second installment in The Word and Void series, and that defines it a little. It is like the third act of any story and gets correspondingly dark. You know, like The Empire Strikes Back. <br /><br />However, I can't decide whether I find John Ross's crisis believable or not. Part of me says that it is over-dramatic and unrealistic for the character that we are introduced to in Running with the Demon to become so self-deceived and self-indulgent and just so plain stupid and pig-headed as John is in this novel. But another part of me says that when people are determined to go astray, when they first make that decision to indulge in self-pity and stubborn denial, they act in that exact way: willing to believe anything and everything that justifies their actions and decisions. So I feel very ambivalent toward John in this book. Either Brooks writes him completely out of character, or this is a stunningly accurate portrait of humanity. His character does grow and mature in the end and that does help. <br /><br />Also, sometimes Brooks baffles me as an author. I am not sure what he is trying to accomplish with the reader. I feel the audience knows the key piece of information in the story well before any of the players, and I know that authors often do this on purpose to heighten the tension. Brooks' hints are broad and hard to miss, but I get the sense that he is teasing the reader. Its like that guy who tells you the really obvious joke or pun and when you don't laugh, says "do ya get it? do ya get it?" I don't understand why he tries to build suspense after he has already revealed so much. Its confusing. <br /><br />But the plot isn't bad, and he does some good character work. I am not saying that I like the characters per se, or that I find in them what I expect from a fantasy novel, but that isn't necessarily a bad thing. They are well-written, confused, lost people that are like everyone else, and I don't necessarily think that we are supposed to like them. The universe is good and this idea of a looming post-apocalyptic world is an intriguing one, and though it may not seem like it from this review, I did enjoy the book. I found it worthwhile to struggle through with John until the end.<br /> <br />So if you want a basic genre read where you can just sit down and immerse yourself in a world, this might not be the book for you. But if you are willing to struggle through things with a hero, and watch someone deal with some of the bigger questions in life against a fantasy background, you will enjoy this book. It is meatier and will give you something to sink your teeth into.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8125403743820812196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3482445995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3482445995" />
    <a title="Gareth Otton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8925316-gareth-otton"><img alt="Gareth Otton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551041676p2/8925316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3482445995?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gareth Otton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gareth Otton" href="/user/show/8925316-gareth-otton">Gareth Otton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3482445995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6525326634190262626">If this series was a television show, then this book would be a filler episode. By this, I mean that this story is trading on the characters and settings of the first novel without actually adding anything to the series. The characters end up exactly where they were when we left the first novel which means that this book could be skipped entirely without losing anything.<br/><br/>This is the fourth time I have read this book over the last 20 years and whenever I come back to this series I always forget wh</span>
  <span id="freeText6525326634190262626" style="display:none">If this series was a television show, then this book would be a filler episode. By this, I mean that this story is trading on the characters and settings of the first novel without actually adding anything to the series. The characters end up exactly where they were when we left the first novel which means that this book could be skipped entirely without losing anything.<br /><br />This is the fourth time I have read this book over the last 20 years and whenever I come back to this series I always forget what it's about. Running with the Demon is always clear in my mind, but this one escapes me. On this reread it is clear that this is the reason why; it is a filler novel. It is a nothing story that is interesting for the simple fact that it's set in the same universe as its much stronger predecessor, and also is a stepping stone on the road to Shannara, but offers little else.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I can't even say that this is a story that lets the characters grow because like I said earlier both Nest and John end up exactly where they were at the end of the first novel. Sure, John overcomes a crisis of faith, but if this novel didn't exist then we wouldn't have worried about that bump in the road. The start of the next novel picks up with the characters exactly how we left them at the last book, with John being a knight of the Word and Nest being… Nest. <br /><br />(Strangely I'm just now realising that despite the fact that Nest is the main character of the series, she doesn't really have much depth to her. John is a knight of the word, his role is very clear in this entire series. Nest is a girl who can run fast and can make people fall down when she looks them in the eye. Her character is set by the end of the first book (as a 14-year old) and she doesn't change much from that. It seems like she's special just because the author wanted her to be special but didn't actually take the time to explain that reason the reader. Why she of all people is an integral part of these big events doesn't make much sense to me now am thinking of it. This clearly isn't a major issue as only just now realising it, but it's food for thought.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This feels like I'm hating on this book but I really don't mean it to come across like that. It's not all awful by any means, and as a stand-alone novel, it's actually quite interesting. The problem is that this isn't a stand-alone novel, it's the middle instalment of a trilogy and on that grounds, it fails.<br /><br />So is three stars for this book, and on to Angel Fire East.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6525326634190262626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2207300037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2207300037" />
    <a title="Dwayne Wojtowicz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34811273-dwayne-wojtowicz"><img alt="Dwayne Wojtowicz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499262396p2/34811273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2207300037?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dwayne Wojtowicz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dwayne Wojtowicz" href="/user/show/34811273-dwayne-wojtowicz">Dwayne Wojtowicz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2207300037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15968391700981648038">“A Knight of the Word” is a fantasy novel by Terry Brooks. The setting is primarily Seattle, Washington around Halloween in 2002. The story follows John Ross as he attempts to leave his service to the Word, while Nest Freemark tries to restore his faith. <br/><br/>I did some research on Brooks before I decided to write this review, being that this is the first book of his that I read. Brooks delves into the world of urban dark fantasy, taking a break from his trademark Tolkienesque adventures.<br/><br/>It has been </span>
  <span id="freeText15968391700981648038" style="display:none">“A Knight of the Word” is a fantasy novel by Terry Brooks. The setting is primarily Seattle, Washington around Halloween in 2002. The story follows John Ross as he attempts to leave his service to the Word, while Nest Freemark tries to restore his faith. <br /><br />I did some research on Brooks before I decided to write this review, being that this is the first book of his that I read. Brooks delves into the world of urban dark fantasy, taking a break from his trademark Tolkienesque adventures.<br /><br />It has been five years since John Ross, a mortal, became a Knight of the Word. His failed attempt to save the lives of children in San Sobel becomes a turning point in his un-volunteered position. He is now considering leaving the order, but has been told that it is not his to give up.<br /><br />Nest Freemark, a college student who has extraordinary magic of her own, has been tapped by The Lady to convince John that he has an obligation to the Word; to save the world from the demons of the Void; she must restore John’s faith, or her and John’s life will be forfeited.<br /><br />Though the vast majority of the book takes place in Seattle, Washington, there are a few scenes that are scripted with Chicago, Illinois (my home town). The story was wonderfully done; however, I felt that some parts dragged, or didn’t have enough exchange between characters.<br /><br />I appreciate the work that Terry Brooks put into the characters. His development of them gave them life beyond other characters I followed. The scenes and transitions between scenes were done beautifully and smoothly. There weren’t any bumps in the road. Though I deal feel that the dialogue between characters could have been pumped up more, all in all, the writing of Terry Brooks receives accolades from me.<br /><br />The story brings in quite of few secondary characters, but Brooks makes it easy to keep them separate from the main characters, and only brought them forth in the story when needed. You, as the reader, did not have to hunt for them. Their dialogue was fine; it could have been a little more descriptive in some areas.<br /><br />The book was wonderfully done. Though fantasy is not a genre that I prefer, Terry Brooks has given me a new perspective on the fantasy genre. I’ll try to get another one of his books on my “to read” list.<br /><br />Recommended to those that love the fantasy genre.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15968391700981648038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3220352221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3220352221" />
    <a title="Sean McBride" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2342151-sean-mcbride"><img alt="Sean McBride" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470234765p2/2342151.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3220352221?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean McBride" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean McBride" href="/user/show/2342151-sean-mcbride">Sean McBride</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3220352221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13622875787283622851">This, the second installment in the Word and the Void trilogy, was just a little pointless. This was a second book filler to bridge a gap to get to the third book. This was a big issue in the Heritage quintet that came previously, where the middle two books were just to fill in what could have been done in one book. The whole point of this book was to show the fallibility of John Ross, the Knight of the Word, for which I can only guess will come into play in Angel Fire East, the last in the Word</span>
  <span id="freeText13622875787283622851" style="display:none">This, the second installment in the Word and the Void trilogy, was just a little pointless. This was a second book filler to bridge a gap to get to the third book. This was a big issue in the Heritage quintet that came previously, where the middle two books were just to fill in what could have been done in one book. The whole point of this book was to show the fallibility of John Ross, the Knight of the Word, for which I can only guess will come into play in Angel Fire East, the last in the Word and Void trilogy. This book did nothing to broaden the originality of Running with the Demon, so it fell flat there and I can only hope that some large shift comes in the next book (in the synopsis, there is mention of a Gypsy Morph, which I know plays a role in future books, so here's to hoping). <br /><br />One more large issue is that Brooks still has not figured out how to create a mystery. Throughout this book there is a question of who the Demon is, but it is painfully apparent from early in the novel, which pilfers any enjoyment from the plot. If you understand who the Demon is, you know exactly how the book will end; which makes it a practice in speed reading.<br /><br />Make no mistake, the writing is getting better. The readability has improved dramatically from the previous series, but Brooks still hits you over the head with his themes and ideas. He needs to practice the art of subtlety and I'd feel comfortable giving this book an extra star, despite the pointlessness of the story. If it is a joy to read, then it doesn't matter nearly as much if it doesn't really add much to the world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13622875787283622851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2988455397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2988455397" />
    <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter"><img alt="Matthew Hunter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495642903p2/3040804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2988455397?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Hunter" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter">Matthew Hunter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2988455397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6087052092220768644">Brooks’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420496.A_Knight_of_the_Word__Word___Void___2_' title='A Knight of the Word (Word & Void, #2) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Knight of the Word</a> has a very different feel than its predecessor, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_' title='Running with the Demon (Word & Void, #1) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Running with the Demon</a>. After being the center of all action in the first installment of the <i>Word & Void</i> series, Sinnissippi Park and Hopewell, Illinois give way to various parks and museums in Seattle. Brooks doesn’t spend near as much time in description mode, allowing the narrative to move along at a faster clip. Personally, I could’ve used more description, and a lot more Pick the Sylvan!<br/><br/>Knight of the Word John Ros</span>
  <span id="freeText6087052092220768644" style="display:none">Brooks’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420496.A_Knight_of_the_Word__Word___Void___2_" title="A Knight of the Word (Word &amp; Void, #2) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">A Knight of the Word</a> has a very different feel than its predecessor, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_" title="Running with the Demon (Word &amp; Void, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Running with the Demon</a>. After being the center of all action in the first installment of the <i>Word &amp; Void</i> series, Sinnissippi Park and Hopewell, Illinois give way to various parks and museums in Seattle. Brooks doesn’t spend near as much time in description mode, allowing the narrative to move along at a faster clip. Personally, I could’ve used more description, and a lot more Pick the Sylvan!<br /><br />Knight of the Word John Ross also goes through a transformation in book 2, becoming less likable, less cool, and much more annoying. I understand having nagging doubts about one’s purpose in life, but subverting your true self and pinning your whole identity to a pretty face with a nice figure? Sure, it happens to Biblical characters like Samson and lovesick teens. But c’mon! John acts like a sap from cover to cover. I like my male heroes with more Marlboro Man and less Robert Smith of the Cure.<br /><br />All that said, I’m enjoying the <i>Word &amp; Void</i> series on the whole, and am interested to see how Brooks connects these prequels to the core <i>Shannara</i> trilogy and beyond. My read through Brooks’s Shannara universe continues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6087052092220768644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2556950512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2556950512" />
    <a title="David Pappas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35241736-david-pappas"><img alt="David Pappas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458653307p2/35241736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2556950512?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Pappas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Pappas" href="/user/show/35241736-david-pappas">David Pappas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2556950512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17505296936585599621">Tempted to give this more than 2 stars, but... Most of the writing is pretty good and he does a decent job of creating a magical world overlay of our own world. With two mostly filled out main characters. Unfortunately there is very little I like worse than an author who feels compelled to jitterbug around in time, mostly in this case to create backstory. Backstory, the outcome to which we as readers we already know - so why bother? What a waste of my time. In fact the author starts the book wit</span>
  <span id="freeText17505296936585599621" style="display:none">Tempted to give this more than 2 stars, but... Most of the writing is pretty good and he does a decent job of creating a magical world overlay of our own world. With two mostly filled out main characters. Unfortunately there is very little I like worse than an author who feels compelled to jitterbug around in time, mostly in this case to create backstory. Backstory, the outcome to which we as readers we already know - so why bother? What a waste of my time. In fact the author starts the book with an episode of backfill which makes many of the immediate subsequent pages quite confusing since the expectation of an apocalyptic world appearing goes unfulfilled. There is an almost interesting plot buried somewhere here in the juking and jiving, but not enough of one to rivet me to my seat. Also unfortunately the bad guy, so to speak, is all too easy to identify early on, so any suspense beyond the chase in the park is blunted. Ehhh...it was almost okay as entertainment. It was better when I began just skipping the backstory chapters entirely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17505296936585599621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9870345424648" href="/book/show/13549235-a-knight-of-the-word">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22590771-todd?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770564120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7688802953846801781">Of the Shannara prequels, this is the best I've read so far, though of course, a reader will want to at least have read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_' title='Running with the Demon (Word & Void, #1) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Running with the Demon</a> first. In fact, one may wish to read The Word and The Void series first among the prequels. It picks up a few years after Running with the Demon and involves some of the same characters and has some interesting plot developments and character growth, with a good amount of action to keep it interesting. Brooks foreshadows pretty heavily, so there aren't to</span>
  <span id="freeText7688802953846801781" style="display:none">Of the Shannara prequels, this is the best I've read so far, though of course, a reader will want to at least have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187124.Running_with_the_Demon__Word___Void___1_" title="Running with the Demon (Word &amp; Void, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Running with the Demon</a> first. In fact, one may wish to read The Word and The Void series first among the prequels. It picks up a few years after Running with the Demon and involves some of the same characters and has some interesting plot developments and character growth, with a good amount of action to keep it interesting. Brooks foreshadows pretty heavily, so there aren't too many genuine surprises, but he keeps the reader waiting for him to go ahead and say it out loud, confirming the reader's suspicions. A reasonably fun and rewarding read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7688802953846801781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This book is better than the one before it, I think - Terry gets better with each book that he writes, in my opinion. <br/> John Ross has declared that he is no longer a Knight of Word, but the mantle of magic is not one that can be cast off by him, alone. He must be released from his service, and the Word still has great need of him, however, the Void has gained part of his trust and is working to turn John Ross to darkness and evil. Nest Freemark is John's </span>
  <span id="freeText13425483926288134414" style="display:none">The second book in the Word/Void Trilogy. This book is better than the one before it, I think - Terry gets better with each book that he writes, in my opinion. <br /> John Ross has declared that he is no longer a Knight of Word, but the mantle of magic is not one that can be cast off by him, alone. He must be released from his service, and the Word still has great need of him, however, the Void has gained part of his trust and is working to turn John Ross to darkness and evil. Nest Freemark is John's only hope. She hasn't seen John or heard from him in the five years since they were last together, but she feels that she owes John. Her race to save John's soul is going to cost her dearly, but it is a price that she is willing to pay to save the Knight of the Word.</span>

<div id="review_2993997059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2993997059" />
    <a title="Flawed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38436950-flawed"><img alt="Flawed" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2993997059&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2993997059" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4710728270948159807">Years ago, John Ross's intervention turned Nest Freemark from the path of the Void. Now she finds herself commissioned by the Word to return the favor. John Ross has given up on the endless pain of service to the Word and is making a life for himself in Seattle.<br/><br/>But Nest isn't the only being with an interest in a former Knight of the Word.<br/><br/>Brooks brings his intensely detailed sense of place to Seattle successfully. The offices of the nonprofit where Ross works are brought to life, peopled by his c</span>
  <span id="freeText4710728270948159807" style="display:none">Years ago, John Ross's intervention turned Nest Freemark from the path of the Void. Now she finds herself commissioned by the Word to return the favor. John Ross has given up on the endless pain of service to the Word and is making a life for himself in Seattle.<br /><br />But Nest isn't the only being with an interest in a former Knight of the Word.<br /><br />Brooks brings his intensely detailed sense of place to Seattle successfully. The offices of the nonprofit where Ross works are brought to life, peopled by his coworkers, his lover, his boss - people who work in humanity's cause. Without the nightmare trials of a Knight. It seems ideal, if only it could last.<br /><br />This book telegraphs pretty hard but I don't even care because a Brooks execution is worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4710728270948159807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369751148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12940660210230976256">A great follow up to Running, thankfully not as slow to get going. When I hit about 40% through I couldn't put the book down. A different location, but the same heroes and man's demons creating chaos. As always Terry Brooks characters are always battling themselves mentally. What I like about these books is that you can see parallels in the world around us in the battle between good and evil...the events on the news that make you think how can people be so evil...Are there demons out there? A wa</span>
  <span id="freeText12940660210230976256" style="display:none">A great follow up to Running, thankfully not as slow to get going. When I hit about 40% through I couldn't put the book down. A different location, but the same heroes and man's demons creating chaos. As always Terry Brooks characters are always battling themselves mentally. What I like about these books is that you can see parallels in the world around us in the battle between good and evil...the events on the news that make you think how can people be so evil...Are there demons out there? A walk through the park will never be the same, as you look for the feeders...or will you sense the demon stink. A great book, onto the next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12940660210230976256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9DYbSis5UFuDDBvBUBgj8x1yx3CccepOIV2K8O7NsHmyoEatK1+KZ3bkBR5jrfKJEbTdRgOKEbvuuM0A2zFD4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zLmxrJJqcts1vHPcN4GzmlB1qdtMkiJxgvzuHnKQMBSKL+xLkgyo58BUbQMENGLgXLOz7dNp2YRNGanuR2zDjA==')})
  }

A. Salvatore set a new standard for fantasy adventure, creating the enchanted world of Corona--a world besieged by the dark forces of an ancient, all-consuming evil. Now, with The Demon Apostle, Salvatore brings his epic symphony of good versus evil to its stunning conclusion.It is a time of mourning. A time of hope. With the demon dactyl and its foul minions defeated, the war-weary citizens of the kingdom of Honce-the-Bear wish only to bury their dead and begin rebuilding their broken lives. Yet the fragile balance between church and state lies shattered. The specter of civil war haunts the ravaged land--and a specter more fearsome still. For the demon, though defeated, was not destroyed. And now its vengeful spirit has found an unholy sanctuary at the very heart of the Abellican Church.As the elf-trained ranger Elbryan Wynden presses north to reclaim the savage Timberlands from retreating goblin hordes, and his companion, Pony, mistress of gemstone magic, turns south to the civilized--but no less perilous--streets of Palmaris, they find themselves caught up in a ruthless power struggle to decide the fate of all Corona. A struggle that will push their courage and love to the breaking point . . . and beyond.Condemned as heretics, the two heroes are hunted by dangerous enemies. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11732248401718817806">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word & Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his</span>
  <span id="freeText11732248401718817806" style="display:none">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word &amp; Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his graduate degree from the School of Law at Washington &amp; Lee University.<br />A writer since high school, he wrote many stories within the genres of science fiction, western, fiction, and non-fiction, until one semester early in his college years he was given The Lord of the Rings to read. That moment changed Terry's life forever, because in Tolkien's great work he found all the elements needed to fully explore his writing combined in one genre.<br />He then wrote The Sword of Shannara, the seven year grand result retaining sanity while studying at Washington &amp; Lee University and practicing law. It became the first work of fiction ever to appear on the New York Times trade paperback bestseller list, where it remained for over five months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11732248401718817806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Now, in Running with the<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText18060194554126060735\" style=\"display:none\">Twenty years ago, Terry Brooks turned fantasy fiction on its head with The Sword of Shannara, the first fantasy novel to make the mainstream bestseller lists, and the first in an unbroken string of thirteen bestselling books. Now, in Running with the Demon, Brooks does nothing less than revitalize fantasy fiction again, inventing the complex and powerful new mythos of the Word and the Void, good versus evil still, but played out in the theater-in-the-round of the &quot;real world&quot; of our present. \n\nOn the hottest Fourth of July weekend in decades, two men have come to Hopewell, Illinois, site of a lengthy, bitter steel strike. One is a demon, dark servant of the Void, who will use the anger and frustration of the community to attain a terrible secret goal. The other is John Ross, a Knight of the Word, a man who, while he sleeps, lives in the hell the world will become if he fails to change its course on waking. Ross has been given the ability to see the future. But does he have the power to change it?\n\nAt stake is the soul of a fourteen-year-old girl mysteriously linked to both men. And the lives of the people of Hopewell. And the future of the country. This Fourth of July, while friends and families picnic in Sinnissippi Park and fireworks explode in celebration of freedom and independence, the fate of Humanity will be decided . . .\n\nA novel that weaves together family drama, fading innocence, cataclysm, and enlightenment, Running with the Demon will forever change the way you think about the fantasy novel. As believable as it is imaginative, as wondrous as it is frightening, it is a rich, exquisitely-written tale to be savored long after the last page is turned.<\/span>\n  <a
